  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bfe2f14c-459f-4ec6-8cc5-335c0e5c6f96'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

If you only want a collect<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I don't know that he has original catchy phrases like this one, but he does elaborate on the reality of this one at length. If you only want a collection of short phrases like that, you can just read proverbs. He quotes that quite extensively.<br /><br />This book is not meaty, though. If you're curious then get it from a library and skim it in an evening. That's what I did!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <a title="Chad Warner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1586355-chad-warner"><img alt="Chad Warner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546011101p2/1586355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75607828?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chad Warner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chad Warner" href="/user/show/1586355-chad-warner">Chad Warner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 0020049024065" href="/book/show/1100324.The_Total_Money_Makeover">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1586355-chad-warner?shelf=finance">finance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1586355-chad-warner?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75607828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer451690720952233904">Ramsey presents some sound financial principles in the book, but it came across as a sales pitch because he mentions his other books and live events, and practically every other page contains a lengthy testimonial from people gushing about their Total Money Makeover. I skipped all of these since I'm looking for practical financial advice, not feel-good stories.<br/><br/>I respect Dave Ramsey as a person and agree with many (maybe most) of his financial principles, but I didn't like Ramsey's strict no-debt</span>
  <span id="freeText451690720952233904" style="display:none">Ramsey presents some sound financial principles in the book, but it came across as a sales pitch because he mentions his other books and live events, and practically every other page contains a lengthy testimonial from people gushing about their Total Money Makeover. I skipped all of these since I'm looking for practical financial advice, not feel-good stories.<br /><br />I respect Dave Ramsey as a person and agree with many (maybe most) of his financial principles, but I didn't like Ramsey's strict no-debt stance. The only exception he allows for is a 15-year fixed-rate mortgage. Although I agree that most people are better off avoiding credit cards because they can't resist the temptation to abuse them, I like to use cash-back and other rewards cards to pay for the things I'd be purchasing anyway. I don't think I spend more money simply because I charge purchases rather than dropping cash or using my debit card. For example, I paid my college tuition on my credit card and earned 1% cash back on thousands of dollars. I also charge all my gas purchases, and make 5% cash back. Did I spend more on tuition or drive more than necessary because I had charged those purchases instead of paying cash? I didn't perform a scientific experiment to determine that, but I'd guess not.<br /><br />I've also <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2164260155" rel="nofollow noopener">reviewed the abridged audio version</a>.<br /><br /><b>The Steps of the Total Money Makeover</b><br /><br /><b>1. Set up a $1000 emergency cash fund</b><br /> Sacrifice, work extra hours, and sell stuff to get the money.<br /> Keep as paper bills or in a savings account.<br /> Don't put it in checking or any other account or investment.<br /><br /><b>2. Pay off your debt snowball</b><br /> List your debts, smallest to largest.<br /> Pay them off.<br /><br /><b>3. Finish the emergency fund</b><br /> Must cover 3 - 6 months of living expenses. 3 months if you have a truly steady job, otherwise 6 months.<br /> $5,000 - $25,000<br /> Put in Money Market with no penalties and check-writing abilities<br /><br /><b>4. Invest 15% of gross income in retirement</b><br /> Don't count any company-matched funds.<br /> Don't count on Social Security.<br /> Use these accounts, in this order:<br /> 1. 401K if company matches.<br /> 2. Roth IRA.<br /> 3. growth-stock mutual funds:<br /> 25% large cap<br /> 25% mid cap<br /> 25% international<br /> 25% small/emerging<br /><br /><b>5. Save for college for your kids</b><br /> Use these accounts, in this order:<br /> 1. Educational Savings Account (ESA) in a growth-stock mutual fund<br /> 2. If you want to save more, use a flexible 529 that allows you to choose your funds<br /> 3. Scholarships <br /><br /><b>6. Pay off the house mortgage</b><br /> Spend every extra dollar you have left after setting aside for living, retirement, college, and mortgage.<br /> Don't keep a low-rate mortgage just so you can invest at a higher rate. After you pay taxes on your investment returns, and factor in the additional risk that the mortgage debt brings, it's not worth it. In the long term, you'll come out ahead by being debt-free.<br /><br /><b>7. Build wealth</b><br /> At this point, you're completely debt-free.<br /> The next step is the Pinnacle Point: when your money makes more than you do.<br /> There are 3 good uses for money:<br /> 1. Fun<br /> Guilt-free enjoyment, if you can afford it.<br /> 2. Investing<br /> Think long-term.<br /> Don't try to time the market.<br /> Choose simple mutual funds and debt-free real estate.<br /> 3. Giving<br /> Giving it away can be the most fun you have with your money.<br /><br /><b>Additional advice</b><br />Winning at money is 80% behavior and 20% head knowledge.<br />"If you will live like no one else, later you can live like no one else."<br />Debt brings risk, not prosperity. You can't leverage debt to build wealth.<br />You don't need to build credit because you won't use it if you follow the Total Money Makeover.<br />Credit card rewards aren't worth it. You end up spending more in unnecessary purchases and interest payments than you make back in rewards. No one ever became rich from credit card rewards.<br /><br />Choose high deductibles for auto and home insurance.<br />Make a will.<br />Choose a term policy, not Whole Life or Universal Life insurance.<br />Don't prepay your kids' college expenses. You'll make higher returns by putting this money in mutual funds.<br />Buy a house for 100% down, or if that's absolutely not possible, get a 15-year fixed-rate mortgage.<br /><br />You don't have to wait until retirement to do what you love. Get a job that you enjoy.<br />A college education improves the quality of your adult life and career. But, it doesn't ensure a job or success.<br />If you have cash or a scholarship, go to college. But pay cash; avoid student loans.<br /><br />Don't get a 30-year mortgage with the intention of paying it off in 15 years. You'll find other things to spend your money on. Having a 15-year mortgage forces you to pay off your home in 15 years.<br />Don't pay points on your mortgage, since you're just paying interest up front.<br />Your house payment should be less than 25% of your take-home pay.<br /><br />Don't lend to friends. If you must give your friends money, give it as a gift. Loans ruin friendships.<br />"Wealth will make you more of what you are", whether you're a jerk or a generous person.<br />"The love of money, not money, is the root of all evil." You have a duty to possess wealth to ensure that it's used properly.<br /><br /><b>Recommended percentages for allocating your money</b><br />Charitable Giving 10-15<br />Saving 5-10<br />Housing 25-35<br />Utilities 5-10<br />Food 5-15<br />Transportation 10-15<br />Clothing 2-7<br />Medical/Health 5-10<br />Personal 5-10<br />Recreation 5-10<br />Debts 5-10</span>
  <a data-text-id="451690720952233904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2030556412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030556412" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2030556412?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=self-improvement">self-improvement</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2030556412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3131346139627787250">Recently, a good friend of mine who knew that I had read this book asked me whether or not I found it helpful. This friend has struggled with managing her personal finances and is drowning in credit card debt. She was feeling pretty hopeless and was worried that she'd never be able to take care of her bills and set enough aside for retirement. <br/><br/>Rather than go into the ins and outs of the book, I downloaded the audiobook version and we listened together while working on paperwork during the work d</span>
  <span id="freeText3131346139627787250" style="display:none">Recently, a good friend of mine who knew that I had read this book asked me whether or not I found it helpful. This friend has struggled with managing her personal finances and is drowning in credit card debt. She was feeling pretty hopeless and was worried that she'd never be able to take care of her bills and set enough aside for retirement. <br /><br />Rather than go into the ins and outs of the book, I downloaded the audiobook version and we listened together while working on paperwork during the work day. Honestly, I just didn't think I could communicate the underlying message of the book without coming across kind of "preachy". This provided a nice way to share the major concepts of the book with her, while providing a strong reminder for me.<br /><br />As you can imagine, personal finance isn't exactly the most entertaining topic. That is especially true when the take away message is to exercise restraint and behave responsibly. Nobody wants to face the fact that we are to blame for our own financial situations. It is far less painful to blame somebody else for the damage we do to ourselves.<br /><br />That being said, I really like Dave Ramsey's common sense approach. He tells some hard truths and forces you to take a long, hard look in the mirror. If you're looking for excuses or a pity party, you won't find it here. He is brutally honest. <br /><br />Sacrifice today for wealth tomorrow is idea. There is no get rich quick scheme presented, just old-fashioned wisdom. Essentially, his advice is to turn back the hands of time and handle money the way my grandparent's generation, and the generations before theirs, did. Don't spend money that you don't have. Save for future expenditures. Quit trying to keep up with the Joneses. It's that simple.<br /><br />Of course, he does provide guidance for how to get out of debt if you've already accumulated it. His personal story of bankruptcy and how he was able to turn around his finances was inspirational. He made it clear that anyone could do it, but they had to be willing to work hard and make some sacrifices. Most importantly, they would have to evaluate their attitudes toward money and be willing to make some changes in their behavior.<br /><br />Although I'm not a very religious person, I wasn't bothered by the bible verses that were interspersed throughout the book. Some people might be put off by that, but it wasn't an issue for me. Clearly, his religious views are an important piece of his identity. For people that are more spiritual than I am, this might prove to be a great source of inspiration. It was neither here nor there for me.<br /><br />All in all, I think that this is a great book. It didn't feel gimmicky or too good to be true. There were no promises or schemes presented. It was just good, sound advice for eliminating debt and living within your means. <br /><br />In fact, I'll probably make my children listen to this as they get older. I'm planning to purchase the book he wrote with his daughter that is geared toward children as well. Might as well start early.<br /><br />Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3131346139627787250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_13585964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/13585964" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/798115-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249255632p2/798115.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/13585964?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/798115-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer13585964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1097418102525590308">I read Financial Peace years ago. We tried to live the plan, but looking back we could have done a lot better. The Total Money Makeover takes the same plan and breaks it down into more detailed babysteps. This REALLY works! We've had our $1000 emergency saving account for years now and have hardly had to dip into it because we really think through what an emergency is. Most of the time we have been able to wait a few weeks until the "extra paycheck," tax return or a bonus comes through instead o</span>
  <span id="freeText1097418102525590308" style="display:none">I read Financial Peace years ago. We tried to live the plan, but looking back we could have done a lot better. The Total Money Makeover takes the same plan and breaks it down into more detailed babysteps. This REALLY works! We've had our $1000 emergency saving account for years now and have hardly had to dip into it because we really think through what an emergency is. Most of the time we have been able to wait a few weeks until the "extra paycheck," tax return or a bonus comes through instead of using our savings. The debt snowball really works. I was amazed when I saw how much money is going toward our last debt! It will only be a few more months to get it paid off. Yes, we did stop retirement for the past year--it was a simple form to fill out at work and only took a couple minutes. The money that was previously in our IRA is still growing, but we're not adding to it right now. When that debt is gone and we have our 3-6 month savings we'll start it up again. What doesn't make sense is having debt when you retire and using your money from your 401K/IRA to pay off the debt.<br /><br />This book is just common sense in a big way! There is so much peace in being in control of our money and our marriage is so much better because we have GOALS that we plan together. <br /><br />This book is a great gift for college graduations and weddings! We buy it on Dave Ramsey's website when it goes on sale for $10 a copy.<br /><br />Update: June 2018.<br />I wrote the original post Jan 2008. We still follow this plan. We've been debt free for the past 10 years. no credit cards for even longer. My husband started his own company--debt free and has never borrowed money for it. We paid for six vehicles in cash (a "dave" car for my husband, a family can, then a truck to replaced the "Dave" vehicle, one replaced the worn out family vehicle, the others are the high schoolers and a college car. Currently have 4 good running, paid for vehicles). We have paid college tuition, missionary support and cash flowed a wedding. Our only debt is our house. It will get more attention after our children are grown. We've been amazed at what we can do by being intentional and planning large purchases, vacations and budgeting!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1097418102525590308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1364062644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1364062644" />
    <a title="Anita L." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45978243-anita-l"><img alt="Anita L." src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1364062644?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anita L." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anita L." href="/user/show/45978243-anita-l">Anita L.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1364062644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17829581076627056985">This book is great for those who are in debt because of overspending. Unfortunately Dave Ramsey groups everyone in the same category with the undisciplined, regardless of their background. He uses unrealistic examples of people having a mortgage of $50,000, or someone paying $250/month for a small apartment while paying off debt. He uses examples of young people in their mid-twenties making $50,000 a year. These are completely unrealistic numbers in most regions of the country.<br/><br/>He proudly says th</span>
  <span id="freeText17829581076627056985" style="display:none">This book is great for those who are in debt because of overspending. Unfortunately Dave Ramsey groups everyone in the same category with the undisciplined, regardless of their background. He uses unrealistic examples of people having a mortgage of $50,000, or someone paying $250/month for a small apartment while paying off debt. He uses examples of young people in their mid-twenties making $50,000 a year. These are completely unrealistic numbers in most regions of the country.<br /><br />He proudly says that his business is debt-free. Dave Ramsey is not a dentist or a chiropractor or a manufacturing business owner who would need expensive equipment to run his business.<br /><br />He fails to understand that many people grow up in poverty and are always just barely keeping up with their bills. They may have a mentally ill spouse or child. People face unfair lawsuits, unemployment, death, and other tragedies in life. His self-righteous response is that you should have had your emergency fund in place before these things happened.<br /><br />Many of us are college-educated, frugal, and self-disciplined. We don’t pay for manicures, we cut everybody’s hair in the family, we don’t buy meat, our vacations are mini-vacations within an hour’s drive from our home, we drive 15-year-old cars, and we live in a small condo.<br /><br />Perhaps his most arrogant statement is that “there is no excuse to retire without financial dignity in the United States today.”<br /><br />If you are educated, hard-working, disciplined, and understand how money works, you will waste your money on this book. You can learn a lot more about money and compassion from Suze Orman than from Dave Ramsey. Buy a book by Suze Orman instead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17829581076627056985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People in debt.</span></div>

      Mom (Bonnie)

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15912530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1776153824793521705">I probably should have given this book more than three stars, because it's a good start to figuring out a critical piece of the financial puzzle; getting out of debt. This book is debt-centric, so, if you're in debt, then yes, you really should read this book.<br/><br/>However, while focusing on getting out of debt is a crucially important step of freeing up your income (because if the money you make every month is spent every month, you're not financially fit), there are many aspects of your financial se</span>
  <span id="freeText1776153824793521705" style="display:none">I probably should have given this book more than three stars, because it's a good start to figuring out a critical piece of the financial puzzle; getting out of debt. This book is debt-centric, so, if you're in debt, then yes, you really should read this book.<br /><br />However, while focusing on getting out of debt is a crucially important step of freeing up your income (because if the money you make every month is spent every month, you're not financially fit), there are many aspects of your financial self that are not addressed in this book. And, while Mr. Ramsey would probably tell you that these aspects of your financial self can wait until you're out of debt, I don't think it's wise to procrastinate an awareness of your financial whole.<br /><br />This is not to say that you should rationalize being in debt and/or put off getting out of it; and Mr. Ramsey has a sure-fire way of doing that. So, to the person in debt, the book does contain a money makeover plan; just not a total money makeover plan.<br /><br />If you want a money makeover that is total, you can combine this book with others ... or my sister, Taibi, has recommended a book called "Making the Most of Your Money," and she says it is a "total" guide to managing money. I'm going to read it myself, soon, and I'll let you know how I like it.<br /><br />Other books I would recommend about money; "Money Harmony" by Olivia Mellan, and "Secrets of the Millionaire Mind." I'll post reviews of those separately.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1776153824793521705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_12468619" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12468619" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/385825-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467226075p2/385825.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12468619?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/385825-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 0020049024065" href="/book/show/1100324.The_Total_Money_Makeover">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12468619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11682802385838760273">This guy's claim is basically that the key to accumulating a lot of money is to (1) become debt free, (2) save a sizeable nest egg (3-10k)for the big emergencies that typically send people into debt in the first place, and (3) put the rest of your savings in mutual funds. He's particularly insistent that you suck it up and drive old cars that you've paid cash for rather than make payments on a new car. <br/>Good advice, but it would help if he offered more insights on how to follow it, especially sin</span>
  <span id="freeText11682802385838760273" style="display:none">This guy's claim is basically that the key to accumulating a lot of money is to (1) become debt free, (2) save a sizeable nest egg (3-10k)for the big emergencies that typically send people into debt in the first place, and (3) put the rest of your savings in mutual funds. He's particularly insistent that you suck it up and drive old cars that you've paid cash for rather than make payments on a new car. <br />Good advice, but it would help if he offered more insights on how to follow it, especially since he seems to think that even those deeply in debt can achieve steps (1) and (2)in a year or two. He uses a lot of catch phrases like "live like no one else!" and "save with gazelle-like intensity!" but some more details would go a long way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11682802385838760273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6295474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6295474" />
    <a title="Cori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/248780-cori"><img alt="Cori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356062642p2/248780.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6295474?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cori" href="/user/show/248780-cori">Cori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who don't have their finances in order</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6295474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11221345886462856737">From my blog:<br/><br/>My friend Amanda was nice enough to buy me Dave Ramsey's book. It must mean it's pretty good if someone else is willing to shell out $25.00 to buy you a book on money management! This book was really repetitive, but I thought it was a fantastic planning tool for those of us who aren't making a gobzillion dollars doing...whatever Paris Hilton does, for example. I have a small bit of debt -- mostly due to 2007: The Year of Dental Nightmares -- and literally no savings. I had quite a b</span>
  <span id="freeText11221345886462856737" style="display:none">From my blog:<br /><br />My friend Amanda was nice enough to buy me Dave Ramsey's book. It must mean it's pretty good if someone else is willing to shell out $25.00 to buy you a book on money management! This book was really repetitive, but I thought it was a fantastic planning tool for those of us who aren't making a gobzillion dollars doing...whatever Paris Hilton does, for example. I have a small bit of debt -- mostly due to 2007: The Year of Dental Nightmares -- and literally no savings. I had quite a bit saved up for a while, but my bills started to eat into my nice little nest egg and the next thing I knew it was gone. Anyway, I think Ramsey has some great ideas for getting back on the right track with your money.<br /><br />One thing he does say, over and over again, is that it is not hard to follow his plan, but it's very difficult to actually pull it off. It's not complicated, but it takes determination and focus if you want to get out of debt and start controlling your money, instead of the other way around. He sets out baby steps for a Total Money Makeover, beginning with scrimping and saving until you have a $1,000 emergency fund (Ramsey notes that things like Christmas are not emergencies: "Christmas is not an emergency; it does not sneak up on you. Christmas is always in December, they don't move it, and therefore it's not an emergency." Heh.). Baby step two is to pay off all your debts using a Debt Snowball. Basically you list your debts from smallest to largest, and pay the minimum payments on all but the smallest, to which you devote as much money as you can possibly can. Then, instead of just moving on to the next debt when the first is paid off, you roll over the amount you were paying for the first debt in addition to the minimum payment for the second debt. And so on. It snowballs so that you are paying debts off faster. Seems easy, not sure how the life application will be. The third baby step is to increase the emergency fund to where it could sustain you for three to six months. Baby step four is to invest, which I do a little of right now, and probably won't stop, even though he recommends it. It's too much of a hassle when I'm pretty sure I can climb out of my mini-hole relatively quickly. The next two steps are to save for college (done and done, thank you Grandma), and to pay off the mortgage (which I don't have). But I'm sure they are helpful for parents who own a home.<br /><br />Seriously, though. The people in this book really did some drastic things to get out of debt (they sold cars, houses, first borns, etc.). I'm not nearly in that kind of trouble, but I think using a watered-down version of his money makeover, I can get my credit card and dental bills paid off a lot sooner than I would have without having read this book. I want to be completely credit card free by the new year, and to the point where I am saving some money AND to where I am able to pay for my Scotland trip with cash. I am also going to attempt to budget October, so we'll see how that goes. It terrifies me to think how much I spend eating out. Yikes.<br /><br />Ramsey is a Christian, but I wouldn't expect anyone who isn't to be turned off by anything he has to say. Basically he quotes a few Proverbs and the people in their testimonies thank God. That's about it. I think the book is totally reasonable if you're not a Christian -- it's not preachy at all.<br /><br />I also checked out Ramsey's website, and was able to answer a few of my questions that weren't answered in the book, such as whether or not I should continue tithing while trying to get rid of the debt (answer: although he won't beat you up if you stop, he highly encourages tithing -- if you can't live on 90%, you can't live on 100%). So that was cool, and I think I'll find more info on there about other things should they come up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11221345886462856737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_232935176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/232935176" />
    <a title="McKenzie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4017921-mckenzie"><img alt="McKenzie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291926243p2/4017921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/232935176?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="McKenzie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="McKenzie" href="/user/show/4017921-mckenzie">McKenzie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232935176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12117169793883055198">After hearing about Dave Ramsey from a number of people, I decided to pick this up out of curiosity. I skimmed this book quickly, partly because it is mostly fluff. His crams the book full of testimonials about other families who have gotten out of debt- that's for the outside of the book, not the inside of it. Most of his actual advice (pay for things with cash, don't buy what you can't afford, live below your means, start investing for retirement early) consists of things my parents have been </span>
  <span id="freeText12117169793883055198" style="display:none">After hearing about Dave Ramsey from a number of people, I decided to pick this up out of curiosity. I skimmed this book quickly, partly because it is mostly fluff. His crams the book full of testimonials about other families who have gotten out of debt- that's for the outside of the book, not the inside of it. Most of his actual advice (pay for things with cash, don't buy what you can't afford, live below your means, start investing for retirement early) consists of things my parents have been telling me since they started giving me an allowance. Ramsey is also vague about the actual saving of money- he suggests that everyone can get together $1000 in less than a month for their emergency fund. If people could find instantaneously $1000 of their income they weren't using elsewhere, wouldn't they have avoided falling into debt in the first place? I am glad other people have been able to use this system to get out of debt and put their finances in order, but this book did pretty much nothing for me. I would like to find a book that's more explicit about budgeting and investing, and one that doesn't tell me being in debt is like being fat, or that our government is completely incompetent at every opportunity, or one that doesn't belittle my chosen career path. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12117169793883055198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9933767918150885040">This is a pretty decent plan for getting out of debt and starting to invest. In the time-honored tradition of such self-help books as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4865.How_to_Win_Friends_and_Influence_People' title='How to Win Friends and Influence People by Dale Carnegie' rel='nofollow noopener'>How To Win Friends and Influence People</a>, Ramsey uses personal stories from other people to drive his points home. <br/><br/>But in essence, the plan is like this: <br/>1) stop buying things, sell off everything you don't need, stop using credit cards, etc.<br/>2) save up a $1000 emergency fund<br/>3) throw all possible cash toward paying off your smallest debt<br/>4) once the first debt is pai</span>
  <span id="freeText9933767918150885040" style="display:none">This is a pretty decent plan for getting out of debt and starting to invest. In the time-honored tradition of such self-help books as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4865.How_to_Win_Friends_and_Influence_People" title="How to Win Friends and Influence People by Dale Carnegie" rel="nofollow noopener">How To Win Friends and Influence People</a>, Ramsey uses personal stories from other people to drive his points home. <br /><br />But in essence, the plan is like this: <br />1) stop buying things, sell off everything you don't need, stop using credit cards, etc.<br />2) save up a $1000 emergency fund<br />3) throw all possible cash toward paying off your smallest debt<br />4) once the first debt is paid off, throw all possible cash toward paying off your second smallest debt, and so on until all you have left is your mortgage (if you have one)<br />5) save up a 3-6 month emergency fund<br />6) start a college fund (if you have kids) and pay off your mortgage<br />7) invest, have fun, etc.<br /><br />Oh, and while Ramsey uses some Bible quotes here and there, it's pretty easy to ignore the parts about "God's plan for you" and other religious nonsense, and focus on the financial advice.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everybody</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Yolanda by: </span>
      Misty Green-Brown
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151795661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12414613548699334529">I can not believe that I've spent the last 12 years working in the Accounting field being such a good steward of my employers money but could never get a good grasp on my own money. The Total Money Makeover book has helped me go from paycheck-to-paycheck-thinking to wealth-building-thinking. Once my eyes were opened (I read the book in 2 days) I knew my financial life would never be the same. I asked my husband to read the book and when he started sending me texts like: Do you know that if we in</span>
  <span id="freeText12414613548699334529" style="display:none">I can not believe that I've spent the last 12 years working in the Accounting field being such a good steward of my employers money but could never get a good grasp on my own money. The Total Money Makeover book has helped me go from paycheck-to-paycheck-thinking to wealth-building-thinking. Once my eyes were opened (I read the book in 2 days) I knew my financial life would never be the same. I asked my husband to read the book and when he started sending me texts like: Do you know that if we invest X dollars in a good mutual fund from age 30 to age 70 that it will be around 5.5 million dollars?!! I knew Dave had him hook, line &amp; sinker. A good percentage of our marital issues surrounded money but there are no arguments on that subject anymore. We understand what the short term goal is (get debt free) and what the long term goals are (remain debt free &amp; build wealth) so most of the decisions have already been made. Once we saw what "keeping up with the Joneses" does to your greatest wealth building tool (income), we decided that we could cut our life down to "rice &amp; beans" for 2 to 2 1/2 years, clean up the massive mess we had made, and reclaim the nearly $2,000 per month we were paying on debt. I sure wish we had this book as teenagers/ younger adults, I can only imagine where we would be now. But even still, my son will never remember how his parents where up to their eyeballs in debt. We still have about $35k (down from 73k) in consumer debt to go, but thank God our financial family tree has been changed forever. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12414613548699334529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14155597172455755634">This book is so helpful, straightforward, and inspiring. I have spent my twenties in the misery of consumer debt and student loans. <br/><br/>I am now credit card debt free and am busting up my student loans. <br/><br/>I like his advice. The very first thing you do is to get 1,000 dollars together BEFORE you start tackling your credit cards.   <span id="freeText14155597172455755634" style="display:none">This book is so helpful, straightforward, and inspiring. I have spent my twenties in the misery of consumer debt and student loans. <br /><br />I am now credit card debt free and am busting up my student loans. <br /><br />I like his advice. The very first thing you do is to get 1,000 dollars together BEFORE you start tackling your credit cards. Be aggressive, take a second job, sell your prized possessions, whatever, but get that $1,000. This is not $$ to keep in a checking account but in a savings account and with drawn ONLY FOR AN EMERGENCY.<br /><br />Now you have a buffer for emergencies. Now when the car breaks or a pipe breaks you don't have to break out the credit card, and it is the first step from freeing you from the shackles of debt.<br /><br />Then you order your debts smallest to largest. Once you pay off the smallest, you can take the $$ from the minimum payment and use it to pay off the next smallest debt. It snowballs.<br /><br />I'm a substitute teacher and make a small salary. To be free of the unrelenting hundreds of dollars of credit card debt is the best thing that has happened to me in so long. <br /><br />I am being over dramatic, but I truly feel hope for my financial future since I was about 14. <br /><br />You gotta buy this book. He has a radio show too but I've never listened.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2298826313135758412"><i>I'm temporarily - I hope - departing from my usual review style while life is crazy and we're in the construction zone. I'm trying this rather than no review at all. I'm basically going to make occasional notes as I read, which is not as satisfactory to me, but hopefully they'll still be helpful. </i><br/><br/>5/28/19: I'm not the financial manager for my home. My husband is. But I decided to listen to this book because I've heard good things about Dave Ramsey and his Financial Peace University course. We did</span>
  <span id="freeText2298826313135758412" style="display:none"><i>I'm temporarily - I hope - departing from my usual review style while life is crazy and we're in the construction zone. I'm trying this rather than no review at all. I'm basically going to make occasional notes as I read, which is not as satisfactory to me, but hopefully they'll still be helpful. </i><br /><br />5/28/19: I'm not the financial manager for my home. My husband is. But I decided to listen to this book because I've heard good things about Dave Ramsey and his Financial Peace University course. We didn't take the course at our church because we didn't want to get rid of our credit cards and because we were decently happy with our financial system. However, right now money is a stressor for my husband because we're putting an expensive addition onto our house. So I decided to listen to it. I'm finding it very entertaining, and I am understanding what he's talking about. Which is great, because I've often been confused by the information finance managers have shared with us when we've had meetings with them in the past. I love how Mr. Ramsey outlines a plan with simple (in concept), concrete steps which he insists must be followed in order, no matter where you are in life. I'd recommend this book for anyone with an income. Period. I think I'm going to give it 5 stars because I think it's that good. But I'll be fair and wait until I'm done. Thomas Nelson is a Christian book publisher, but I think it's worth noting that the author rarely makes Christian references, and when it is it's usually a brief verse from the book of Proverbs. Proverbs does have a lot of wise things to say about money, so I think any non-Christian would not be turned off by this book. Now that I'm listening to this book, I'm eager to start our family financial meetings again (with my husband and two oldest children).<br /><br />5/28/19: I finished this today. I think my notes above pretty well sums up my thoughts on the book. I'd like my oldest son, who is nearly 16, to listen to it.</span>

  <span id="freeText7562755198349855848" style="display:none">I was always someone who wanted to manage their personal finance effectively. However, due to my own carelessness or circumstances, I failed to achieve that goal.<br /><br />After reading this book, I actually realized where I was going wrong and how I could ensure financial stability in my life. The book starts off with debunking myths that every individual has with regards to wealth and money usage. <br /><br />The book then goes on to provide 7 steps we can incorporate into our lives to ensure we acquire financial abundance and get out of any debt or financial crisis. <br /><br />The inclusion of testimonies of those who have used and applied the Total Money Makeover Plan intensifies the appeal of the book and gives one hope that there are similar individuals in life who have gone through a hard time and have been able to overcome those difficult times.<br /><br />A great book that youth, businessmen, and all individuals need to read. Most of the stuff that we are taught as school is in reality of no use to us once we start working. The inclusion of subjects such as financial management would greatly influence students and ensure personal as well as financial success.</span>

<div id="review_18083924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18083924" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1003450-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550457666p2/1003450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18083924?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/1003450-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone.  The principles apply to the general population.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jen by: </span>
      A co-worker and good friend
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1003450-jen?shelf=finance">finance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18083924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11783944926549285743">Let me preface this by saying that I'm a <b>HUGE</b> fan of Dave Ramsey, so of course I'm a bit biased. I listen to his talk radio show every day without fail, and I'm an active member of his subscription website called MyTMMO (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.mytotalmoneymakeover.com'>http://www.mytotalmoneymakeover.com</a>).<br/><br/>My husband and I began working the baby steps in September 2005. It took us 22 long months of discipline and sacrifice to become completely debt-free. We don't own a home yet, so yes, we really are living the debt-free life. We paid off more </span>
  <span id="freeText11783944926549285743" style="display:none">Let me preface this by saying that I'm a <b>HUGE</b> fan of Dave Ramsey, so of course I'm a bit biased. I listen to his talk radio show every day without fail, and I'm an active member of his subscription website called MyTMMO (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.mytotalmoneymakeover.com">http://www.mytotalmoneymakeover.com</a>).<br /><br />My husband and I began working the baby steps in September 2005. It took us 22 long months of discipline and sacrifice to become completely debt-free. We don't own a home yet, so yes, we really are living the debt-free life. We paid off more than $36,000 and our income jumped up dramatically during that period of time using Ramsey's baby steps. The last debt was paid off on June 15, 2007 (it was my student loan). I can't even describe how good that felt. We called the talk radio show on July 13, 2007 to proclaim our debt freedom to all of America. Dave does something he calls "Debt Free Fridays" where callers who've paid off all their debts can call in and scream. The show has become a bit famous for it.<br /><br />The principles in Ramsey's book really are simple. And the people who listen to his radio show or watch his TV show on FBN are <b>incredibly</b> loyal to him. What inspires such loyalty? Well, I'd say it's the bluntness, directness, and authenticity of Dave's personality. His slight Tennessee drawl is an effective "I'm just a good ol' boy" tool. He says what he means and means what he says.<br /><br />Yes, Dave is a Christian, and he certainly won't hide it. He isn't "preachy," as someone else said, but if someone asks a question about tithing, he's not going to shy away from it. There are mentions in the book about his Christian roots, but that's just part of his character. And if you're curious about the "baby steps," the name comes from the movie <i>What About Bob?</i> Ramsey often declares his financial principles as God's and Grandma's ways of dealing with money. And he's right. Generations before us really did use these principles. We've just forgotten them as credit cards and loans have become the popular way to pay for things.<br /><br />When Dave says that normal is broke, he isn't kidding. I'm happy to be called "weird."</span>
  <a data-text-id="11783944926549285743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1592125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16929090005594521849">I love Dave Ramsey. We have been doing the Total Money Makeover since Jan 1 of this year (we started after reading Dave's book "Financial Peace") and we are already seeing plenty of success with our baby steps. We pay for everything in cash now and if we don't have the cash, we don't buy it. We've got an emergency fund in place and have used it when things came up - auto repairs, etc. And best of all, we are in debt reduction mode - we had cut up all the credit cards Jan 1 and now we only see ba</span>
  <span id="freeText16929090005594521849" style="display:none">I love Dave Ramsey. We have been doing the Total Money Makeover since Jan 1 of this year (we started after reading Dave's book "Financial Peace") and we are already seeing plenty of success with our baby steps. We pay for everything in cash now and if we don't have the cash, we don't buy it. We've got an emergency fund in place and have used it when things came up - auto repairs, etc. And best of all, we are in debt reduction mode - we had cut up all the credit cards Jan 1 and now we only see balances getting smaller or eliminated.<br /><br />I highly recommend Dave's book. Wish I had found it as a younger person. He writes in an very straight-forward, easy to understand way, without being dry or dull.</span>

<div id="review_2372691881" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2372691881" />
    <a title="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy"><img alt="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475772748p2/4702933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2372691881?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" href="/user/show/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy">MrsJoseph *grouchy*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/24842502-the-total-money-makeover">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=educational">educational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=2018-reading-challenges">2018-reading-challenges</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=2018-tbr-challenge">2018-tbr-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372691881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2242307455901106828">6 years, 3 months<br/><br/>--Pre review --<br/><br/>I'm very familiar with Dave Ramsey (I was introduced to him by my husband). I like both him and Suze Orman (but for different reasons). <br/><br/>This is more of a twofer for me: I get a refresher course on not spending all my damn money AND I knock this book off Mt. TBR. Win/Win.<br/><br/>When I first started listening to Dave's radio show + podcasts (20years+), I was certainly part of his target audience: someone who was never taught about finance and made bad financial decisions. </span>
  <span id="freeText2242307455901106828" style="display:none">6 years, 3 months<br /><br />--Pre review --<br /><br />I'm very familiar with Dave Ramsey (I was introduced to him by my husband). I like both him and Suze Orman (but for different reasons). <br /><br />This is more of a twofer for me: I get a refresher course on not spending all my damn money AND I knock this book off Mt. TBR. Win/Win.<br /><br />When I first started listening to Dave's radio show + podcasts (20years+), I was certainly part of his target audience: someone who was never taught about finance and made bad financial decisions. The only financial knowledge I received prior to college was instructions on how to write a check (no, I didn’t know how to balance a checkbook). When I got to college, credit card companies (they were set up outside the student union and dorms like vultures) quickly taught me more than I wanted to know about finance. I was told that I could get a credit card because my <i>scholarship</i> was the equivalent of income. *headdesk* I had somewhere in the nature of 5 credit cards before I was finished with my first semester of college.<br /><br />Yeah, I had a shitton of debt.<br /><br />Using Dave's very basic and commonsense tools (he says that it's the same advice you'd get from your grandma but he keeps his teeth in, lol), I was able to dig myself out of all my debt. <br /><br />There are somethings he suggests that I do not do - but it's more about personal convenience/laziness rather than a belief that he's incorrect. I have a 30-year mortgage and I use a debit card rather than cash. The emergency fund? I think it is THE MOST IMPORTANT thing he can suggest to anyone, especially humans who live in the world. ;-) The very first year we bought our house we had to replace my car, replace the roof AND replace the A/C. Can you imagine?? We JUST bought the house - can you imagine what it would have been like without an emergency fund? What could have turned into a financial nightmare ended up being an[major] inconvenience. <br /><br />This is not a book or a system for those who want complicated or sophisticated. This is simple math and simple concepts that work. I know for a fact that they work because I've seen my life changed because of them. I know I could do better, though. <i>*whispers* I stop listening to Dave when I want to spend money. </i><br /><br />Note: I really loved the debt free phone calls Dave takes on his show. I miss that here in the book. Those calls - so full of excitement for the future - used to make me a little misty eyed.<br /><br /><br />--After Reading Review –<br /><br />So, I feel a little embarrassed reading this book. We should be firmly in the wealth building stage of our lives but I have a spending PROBLEM. I like stuff – I like the act of buying stuff and I don’t have a saver’s spirit. My husband does but I need a portable budget and constant reminders. CONSTANT.<br /><br />Example: I have a tiny bit of business debt I seriously need to get rid of. It’s bothering my husband like nobody’s business so I really need it gone. But what did I do on Friday? I went to Sephora and bought Illuminator and a lip gloss. $60!!!! That same $60 could have been put towards my debt. Hubby has not a clue I bought it, either. What’s worse is that I didn’t NEED the illuminator or the gloss. I have plenty of illuminator – just not in the shade I wanted (And I’m thinking of taking this back for a different shade but that would be ridiculous because all sorts of complicated makeup reasons). <br /><br />Maybe I need to start listening to the podcast again…<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2242307455901106828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Pamela " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3042834-pamela"><img alt="Pamela " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470806235p2/3042834.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98557965?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela " href="/user/show/3042834-pamela">Pamela </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98557965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3709102133328470012">My husband & I have come up with a budget & decided to follow Dave Ramsey's 7 step plan to become completely debt free, including our mortgage! We are very excited about it! Our goal is to get to the point where we can pay cash for everything, build wealth & plan for retirement by investing, have fun, & give to others. <br/><br/>The great thing about this plan is that it is NOT a "Get-Rich-Quick Scheme". It will take a lot of hard work and sacrifice, but it will be worth it in the end! It is basic, common</span>
  <span id="freeText3709102133328470012" style="display:none">My husband &amp; I have come up with a budget &amp; decided to follow Dave Ramsey's 7 step plan to become completely debt free, including our mortgage! We are very excited about it! Our goal is to get to the point where we can pay cash for everything, build wealth &amp; plan for retirement by investing, have fun, &amp; give to others. <br /><br />The great thing about this plan is that it is NOT a "Get-Rich-Quick Scheme". It will take a lot of hard work and sacrifice, but it will be worth it in the end! It is basic, common sense principals. I like the fact that there's a plan for an emergency fund. You can have a safety net while you are eliminating your debt. <br /><br />First, you have to change your mind-set. Credit cards, student loans, car payments, &amp; even a 30-year mortgage do not have to be the norm. Debt, any debt, is bad. Self-reliance, security, &amp; FREEDOM is something that few people have achieved. <br /><br />ANYONE can do this! It does not matter how much income you have. It does not matter how much debt you are in. You CAN make the change! Make a plan &amp; follow it with "gazelle-like intensity". :)<br /><br />"If you live like no one else, later you can live like no one else!"<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145288178" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14587357929167808211">Thank you Tulsa Blizzard 2011 for helping me finish this book in two days. <br/><br/>What makes this book so effective and successful is that it lays out a very appealing vision, which motivates the reader to make the dramatic changes necessary to become financially secure. By the end of the book, you are motivated and energized to do whatever it takes to achieve the vision of wealth described in this book. The best part is that it’s totally doable and no kind of hoax. Like the author says, there’s no exc</span>
  <span id="freeText14587357929167808211" style="display:none">Thank you Tulsa Blizzard 2011 for helping me finish this book in two days. <br /><br />What makes this book so effective and successful is that it lays out a very appealing vision, which motivates the reader to make the dramatic changes necessary to become financially secure. By the end of the book, you are motivated and energized to do whatever it takes to achieve the vision of wealth described in this book. The best part is that it’s totally doable and no kind of hoax. Like the author says, there’s no excuse for any American not to retire with dignity. <br /><br />Quotes:<br /><br />Only the financial goobers like to complicate things for the sake of justifying their existence or justifying how much they paid for their education.<br /><br />Consumer confidence is that thing economists use to measure how much you will overspend due to your being giddy about how great the economy is, never taking into consideration that you are going deeply into debt.<br /><br />I love my stupid car more than the idea of becoming wealthy enough to give cars away.<br /><br />The USA Today reports that out of one hundred people age sixty-five, ninety-seven of them can’t write a check for $600, fifty-four are still working, and three are financially secure.<br /><br />When selecting and working with your wealth team, it is vital to bring on only members who have the heart of a teacher, not the heart of a salesman or the heart of an “expert...” Also, when taking advice, evaluate if the person giving the advice will profit from the advice.<br /><br />It is the duty of the good people to get wealth to keep it from the bad people, because the good people will do good with it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17261773378326957222">I'm always cautious about books or products which supposedly save you money. What's the old adage? "How do you make a lot of money? Write a book about how to make a lot of money"<br/>This book did that annoying thing where it spends the first few chapters telling you how great the system works, but doesn't give the system out until the second half of the book. I'm not a fan of that particular literary device.<br/>Also, I felt like many pages of "success stories" were overkill. A few would have been great,</span>
  <span id="freeText17261773378326957222" style="display:none">I'm always cautious about books or products which supposedly save you money. What's the old adage? "How do you make a lot of money? Write a book about how to make a lot of money"<br />This book did that annoying thing where it spends the first few chapters telling you how great the system works, but doesn't give the system out until the second half of the book. I'm not a fan of that particular literary device.<br />Also, I felt like many pages of "success stories" were overkill. A few would have been great, but there are so many as to make them superfluous. <br />That said, <br />His principles are sound and anyone encouraging people to get out of debt is fine with me.</span>

<div id="review_2245803286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2245803286" />
    <a title="Melanie Kilsby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32298286-melanie-kilsby"><img alt="Melanie Kilsby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453228973p2/32298286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2245803286?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie Kilsby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie Kilsby" href="/user/show/32298286-melanie-kilsby">Melanie Kilsby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18881132-the-total-money-makeover">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32298286-melanie-kilsby?shelf=books-i-would-read-again">books-i-would-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32298286-melanie-kilsby?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32298286-melanie-kilsby?shelf=christian-non-fiction">christian-non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2245803286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10200218077368641869">Very practical and biblically sound advice!<br/><br/>This book will hit you in the gut and make you shake your head at the same time. It will be hard to listen to and even harder to do. But, will be beneficial to you in the end. <br/><br/>Dave likens a lot of his advice to working out and getting in shape. He paints the view of someone working hard to ride his bike up the mountain, pushing all the way to the top with "gazelle" like attitude. Once there, enjoy the wind and breeze flying down.<br/><br/>I like this book for man</span>
  <span id="freeText10200218077368641869" style="display:none">Very practical and biblically sound advice!<br /><br />This book will hit you in the gut and make you shake your head at the same time. It will be hard to listen to and even harder to do. But, will be beneficial to you in the end. <br /><br />Dave likens a lot of his advice to working out and getting in shape. He paints the view of someone working hard to ride his bike up the mountain, pushing all the way to the top with "gazelle" like attitude. Once there, enjoy the wind and breeze flying down.<br /><br />I like this book for many reasons and already do the concepts presented in this book. We've been applying many of these biblical truths and wisdom from early on in our marriage. It's refreshing to see others doing the same and helping people in the process. <br /><br />What doesn't work for me in the book is that is is solely based off the US economy. <br /><br />His advice is for the average couple or person making $50, 000 per year, give or take. It's impractical when comparing to other places in the world and this is where I see a big difference. <br /><br />When we compare "free money" after the snowball debt and you've saved enough to live off of for 3-6 months, he talks about putting 15% of your income into various things to gain wealth including retirement savings plans (that are also different in other countries - so keep that in mind) and saving for your children's college, etc. From there, it's the last steps into investing where you really build the wealth and have your money working for you. Here is the but...<br /><br />But, in most places, with that income average, there is no "free money" and everything is spoken for because of living expenses. They can get out of debt by a lot of hard work, selling things, etc. But to put %15 away is unrealistic to places where I live compared to where the author lives. <br /><br />When the average in income is approx. the same as US at $50, 000, BUT living expenses are 13 - 21 % more higher on average, what do you do? <br /><br />Here is the latest comparison as of this year 2017 and I feel very accurate: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.expatistan.com/cost-of-living/comparison/nashville/vancouver">https://www.expatistan.com/cost-of-li...</a>?<br /><br />Don't get me wrong. Applying the principles laid out, will benefit you greatly and start the upward climb to getting victory over financial problems. And debt free, no doubt! <br /><br />But if it comes down to living expenses. There is no solid advice, except move from where those living expenses are high.<br /><br />Moving isn't always an option. <br />Nor is commuting. <br /><br />There is a lot to consider with both suggestions...<br /><br />Prices of gas in comparison are 15 - 45% higher in some places and that is not considering wear-n-tear on the vehicle at all. It might mean losing the better paying job to relocate. And in Canada (and for many international areas), job security is sometimes more of a risk when thinking of quitting to relocate and find better housing. It truly can be a gamble with you being on the losing end.<br /><br />So, I wish there was a better portion of this book that spoke to other International places. Or maybe even a book on International economies with wisdom that is biblical and maybe more realistic to those specific countries? <br /><br />Regardless, biblical principles is always the right way to go. We are debt free by doing the very things mentioned in this book. And I am glad to have found someone explaining these ideals for the US and hopefully soon, making them more realistic for others all over the world :D<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10200218077368641869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
